Ruling on Agent Buying/Selling from Those Whose Testimony is Rejected
Expands on prohibition for wakil to transact with close relations and its rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent's transaction with close relations, identify the underlying cause (tamah), and apply the exceptions for mudarib and wasi.

Core Idea
An agent cannot sell to close relations because tamah invalidates—but a mudarib can at market value.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands on a key restriction in agency law. The general rule prohibits an agent from buying or selling from those whose testimony would be rejected in his favor, due to the accusation of partiality. However, exceptions exist for the mudarib and the wasi under specific conditions.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling and its scope
Identify the act (sale/purchase by agent) and the ruling (fasid/invalid). Note that this applies to all contracts like ijarah, sarf, salam, and marriage.
2
Identify the prohibited persons
List the individuals whose testimony is rejected: ascendants, descendants, spouse, master, slave, mukatib, and partner in jointly owned property.
The text says 'like his root and branch' etc.
3
Understand the proof (dalil)
The ruling is based on two proofs: (1) analogy to rejection of testimony between such parties, (2) interconnection of benefits making the transaction akin to self-dealing.
The key phrase: 'haadha mawdi' al-tuhmah'.
4
Distinguish the mudarib exception
The mudarib (manager in mudarabah) can sell at market value by agreement, because he acts for himself in one respect.
The 'illa of tamah does not attach here.
5
Distinguish the wasi exception
The executor (wasi) can sell at market value but cannot show favoritism (muhabah) even if slight.
This is similar to the mudarib but with stricter conditions.

Source Text

فصل في البيع
لا يصح بيع الوكيل وشراؤه من ترد شهادته له
[۱] فصل في البيع
[٤] (لا يصح بيع الوكيل وشراؤه ممن ترد شهادته له) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة ۱ فصل : هذا فصل في بيان أحكام من يجوز للوكيل أن يعقد معه، ومن لا يجوز.
[٢] قوله : بيع الوكيل وشراؤه ؛ وكذا الإجارة والصرف والسلم ونحوها كالتزويج ، فلو وكله بتزويج فزوجه بنته ولو كبيرة، أو من لا تقبل شهادته له لا يجوز. صرح به في «البزازية». وقوله : بيع الوكيل ؛ شمل المضارب إلا إذا كان بمثل القيمة، فإنه يجوز اتفاقاً ؛ لأنه منصرف لنفسه من وجه ، وقيد بالوكيل ؛ لأنَّ الوصي لو باع منهم بمثل القيمة فإنّه يجوز، وإن حابي فيه لا يجوز، وإن قل كالوصي. ذكره العلامة الطحطاوي (1) نقلاً عن «السراج»، وهذا احتراز عن وكيل القبض، كما لو وكل رجلاً بقبض دين على أبيه أو ولده أو مكاتب لولده أو عبده فقال الوكيل : قبضتُ الدين وهلك وكذبه الطالب، فالقول قول الوكيل. كما صرحوا به.
[٣] قوله : ممن ترد شهادته له كأصله وفرعه، وزوجه، وزوجته، وسيده، وعبده، ومكاتبه، وشريكه فيما يشتركانه.
[٤] قوله : هذا عند أبي حنيفة له له إن مواضع التهمة مستثناة عن الوكالات، وهذا موضع التهمة بدليل عدم قبول الشهادة ؛ ولأنَّ المنافع بينهم متصلة، فصار بيعاً من نفسه من وجه، بخلاف المضاربة، فإنَّ المضارب كالمتصرف لنفسه من وجه. ألا ترى أنَّ ربَّ المالَ لا يملك نهيه عن التصرُّف بعدما ضارب المال عروضاً، وإنه شريكه في الربح ، فلا تلحقه التهمة في البيع بمثل القيمة ؛ لأنه بمنزلة من يبيعُ مالَ نفسه
Chapter on sale: It is not valid for the agent to sell or buy from someone whose testimony is rejected for him. This is according to Abu Hanifa. A chapter: This is a chapter explaining the rulings of whom the agent may contract with and whom he may not. His saying: 'The agent's sale and purchase' – likewise ijarah, sarf, salam, and similar contracts like marriage. If he authorized him to marry and he married his daughter, even if adult, or someone whose testimony is not accepted for him, it is not valid. This is stated in al-Bazzaziyya. And his saying: 'The agent's sale' includes the mudarib except if it is at the equivalent value, then it is valid by agreement because he is acting for himself in one respect. And it is restricted to the agent because if the executor sells to them at the equivalent value, it is valid, but if he shows favoritism it is not valid even if little, like the executor. Al-Allama al-Tahatawi mentioned it quoting from al-Siraj. And this is a caution regarding the agent for collection, as if a man authorized a person to collect a debt from his father, son, his son's slave, or his slave, and the agent said 'I collected the debt and it perished' and the claimant denies, then the word is the agent's word, as they stated. His saying: 'From one whose testimony is rejected for him' like his root and branch, his husband, his wife, his master, his slave, his mukatib, and his partner in what they jointly own. His saying: 'This is according to Abu Hanifa' – because the places of accusation are excluded from agencies, and this is a place of accusation evidenced by the rejection of testimony, and because benefits are interconnected among them, so it becomes a sale from himself in a way, unlike mudarabah because the mudarib is like one acting for himself in a way. Do you not see that the owner does not have the power to prohibit him from disposing after he has given the goods as capital, and he is his partner in profit, so accusation does not attach to selling at the equivalent value because he is like one selling his own property.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's ruling regarding the agent's sale to those from whom his testimony is rejected. The commentator begins by stating the general ruling: it is not valid for the agent to buy or sell from close relations whose testimony would not be accepted in his favor, such as his ascendants, descendants, spouse, master, slave, mukatib, and partner in jointly owned property. This ruling, attributed to Abu Hanifa, is based on the principle that places of tamah (accusation of partiality) are excluded from agency. The proof is twofold: the rejection of testimony between such parties and the interconnection of benefits, which makes the sale akin to selling one's own property. The commentator then distinguishes the general agent from the mudarib (silent partner in mudarabah), for whom selling at market value is permissible by agreement (ittifaqan) because he has a dual role as both agent and owner-like figure. Similarly, the executor (wasi) can sell at market value but cannot show favoritism. The text also clarifies that this ruling applies to various contracts like ijarah, sarf, salam, and marriage. Additionally, there is a special case of an agent authorized to collect a debt: if he claims to have collected and lost the money, his word is accepted due to the nature of the agency. The commentator emphasizes that the prohibition is due to tamah, and it does not apply to mudarib when selling at market price because he is effectively selling his own property.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): Someone appointed to act on behalf of another in legal transactions like sale, purchase, marriage, etc. The text specifically excludes mudarib and wasi from the general prohibition in certain cases.
تهمة (tuhmah): Accusation of partiality or bias due to close relationship or interconnected interests, which serves as the 'illa for invalidating the agent's transaction with certain individuals.
مضارب (mudarib): The manager in a mudarabah (profit-sharing) partnership. The text exempts him from the prohibition when selling at market value, because he is considered to be acting for himself in one respect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible for a mudarib to buy from or sell to someone whose testimony is rejected for him?
A) Under no circumstances
B) Only if the transaction is at the equivalent market value
C) If the principal explicitly permits it
D) Only if the mudarib is also the owner of the goods

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts an agent's transactions with close relations due to tuhmah, but the mudarib can transact at market value because he has a dual role.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Agent Selling to Relatives: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Suspicion (Tuhma)
Expands ruling on agent's sales to relatives and the intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on an agent selling to close relatives, identify the key reasoning (tuhma vs. custom), and apply the ruling to a real-life scenario.

Core Idea
An agent cannot sell to close relatives if suspicion exists; Abu Hanifa forbids it absolutely, but the Sahibayn allow it at fair market value.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of an agent (wakil) selling to or buying from persons whose testimony would be rejected for him due to close relationship. The disagreement turns on whether such transactions inherently involve suspicion (tuhma) or can be conducted without conflict of interest. We will analyze the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, al-Sahibayn, and the practical implications for everyday transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited persons
List the individuals for whom testimony is rejected (father, son, spouse, master, slave, mukatab, partner). Understand that these are 'places of suspicion'.
The list is exhaustive for the doctrine of tuhma.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's absolute prohibition
Explain why Abu Hanifa deems all such sales invalid: connected benefits (al-manafi' muttasila) make it a sale from oneself; testimonial rejection evidences suspicion.
Note the exception: mudarib selling at like value is valid by agreement.
3
Contrast the Sahibayn's conditional permission
State the conditions: sale at fair market value (mithl al-qima) and for cash (dirhams/dinars) or customary credit. Explain their reasoning: separate ownerships (al-amlak mutabayina) and disconnected benefits remove suspicion.
Use the concubine example to illustrate separate ownerships.
4
Examine the evidence and analogies
Analyze the arguments: Abu Hanifa uses testimonial rejection as evidence of tuhma; Sahibayn analogize to married couples' separate property and distinguish the case of slaves.
The slave case is invalid because the master owns what the slave possesses.
5
Determine the practical difference
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, the transaction must be done by the principal; under the Sahibayn, the agent can proceed if conditions are met.
Mufta bihi typically favors the Sahibayn for ease.

فصل في البيع (لا يصح بيع الوكيل وشراؤه ممن ترد شهادته له) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة. هذا فصل في بيان أحكام من يجوز للوكيل أن يعقد معه، ومن لا يجوز. قوله : بيع الوكيل وشراؤه ؛ وكذا الإجارة والصرف والسلم ونحوها كالتزويج ، فلو وكله بتزويج فزوجه بنته ولو كبيرة، أو من لا تقبل شهادته له لا يجوز. صرح به في «البزازية». وقوله : بيع الوكيل ؛ شمل المضارب إلا إذا كان بمثل القيمة، فإنه يجوز اتفاقاً ؛ لأنه منصرف لنفسه من وجه ، وقيد بالوكيل ؛ لأنَّ الوصي لو باع منهم بمثل القيمة فإنّه يجوز، وإن حابي فيه لا يجوز، وإن قل كالوصي. ذكره العلامة الطحطاوي نقلاً عن «السراج»، وهذا احتراز عن وكيل القبض، كما لو وكل رجلاً بقبض دين على أبيه أو ولده أو مكاتب لولده أو عبده فقال الوكيل : قبضتُ الدين وهلك وكذبه الطالب، فالقول قول الوكيل. كما صرحوا به. قوله : ممن ترد شهادته له كأصله وفرعه، وزوجه، وزوجته، وسيده، وعبده، ومكاتبه، وشريكه فيما يشتركانه. قوله : هذا عند أبي حنيفة له؛ له إن مواضع التهمة مستثناة عن الوكالات، وهذا موضع التهمة بدليل عدم قبول الشهادة ؛ ولأنَّ المنافع بينهم متصلة، فصار بيعاً من نفسه من وجه، بخلاف المضاربة، فإنَّ المضارب كالمتصرف لنفسه من وجه. ألا ترى أنَّ ربَّ المالَ لا يملك نهيه عن التصرُّف بعدما ضارب المال عروضاً، وإنه شريكه في الربح ، فلا تلحقه التهمة في البيع بمثل القيمة ؛ لأنه بمنزلة من يبيعُ مالَ نفسه. (وصح بيع الوكيل بما قل أو كثر، والعرض، والنسيئة)، هذا عند أبي حنيفة ، وعندهما : لا يصح إلا بما يتغابنُ النَّاسُ فيه، فلا يصح إلا بالدراهم والدنانير؛ لأن المطلق ينصرف إلى المتعارف ، والمراد بالنسيئة : البيع بالثمن المؤجل، وعندهما يتقيد بأجل متعارف. قوله : عندهما؛ إن التوكيل مطلق عن التقييدِ بشخص دون شخص ، ولا تهمة في البيع بمثل القيمة ؛ لأن الأملاك متباينة، والمنافع منقطعة. ألا ترى أنه يحل للابن وطء جاريته، ولو لم يكن ملكه مبايناً عن ملك أبيه لكانت جارية مشتركة، ولم يحل له وطؤها حينئذ بخلاف العبد ؛ لأنَّ البيع من عبده بيع نفسه ؛ لأنَّ ما في يد العبدِ للمولى ، فصار الواحد متولياً طرفي العقد، وذا لا يجوز، وللمولى حق في مال مكاتبه، وينقلب حقيقة بالعجز ، فيكون بيعاً من نفسه أو تمكنت شبهة، وبخلاف الغبن الفاحش. قوله : وعندهما لا يصح ...الخ ؛ يعني إنَّ عندهما وهـو قـول الشافعي له أيضاً ، لا يصح بيعه بنقصان لا يتغابنُ النَّاسُ فيه، فيجوز بالغبن اليسير، ولا يجوز بيعه إلا بالدراهم والدنانير حالة، أو إلى أجل متعارف ؛ لأن التوكيل بالبيع وقع مطلقاً، والمطلق ينصرف إلى المتعارف، فيتقيد به. والسر فيه : إنَّ التصرفات إنّما وُضِعَتْ لدفع الحاجات، فالتوكيل بالتصرفاتِ تتقيد بمواقع الحاجة، والمتعارفُ هو البيعُ بثمن المثل وبالنقود حالة أو مؤجلة بأجل متعارف بين الناس، وبيع ما يساوي ألفا بعشرة إلى مئة سنة مثلاً غير متعارف. ألا ترى أن التوكيل بشراء الفحم يتقيد بأيام البرد في تلك السنة، والتوكيلُ بشراء الحمد بأيام الصيف في تلك السنة، والتوكيل بشراء الأضحية بأيام النحر في تلك السنة أو قبلها، حتى لو اشترى ذلك في السنة الثانية لم يلزم الآمر ، صرح به في «العناية» وغيرها.
Chapter on Sales. (It is not valid for the agent to sell or buy from someone whose testimony is rejected for him.) This is according to Abu Hanifa. This chapter is an explanation of the rulings of whom the agent is allowed to contract with and whom not. His statement: 'the agent's selling and buying'—and likewise leasing, currency exchange, salam, and similar contracts like marriage. So if he appoints him to marry, and he marries him to his daughter, even if she is an adult, or to someone whose testimony is not accepted for him, it is not valid. This is explicitly stated in al-Bazzaziyya. His statement: 'the agent's selling' includes the mudarib (investment agent) except when it is at like value, then it is valid by agreement because he is acting for himself from one aspect. And it is restricted to the agent because if the executor (wasi) sells to them at like value, it is valid, and if he is lenient it is not valid, even if it is little like the executor. Al-Tahtawi mentioned it quoting from al-Siraj. And this is a caution regarding an agent for collection (wakil al-qabd), as when a man appoints an agent to collect a debt from his father or his child or his son's mukatab or his slave, and the agent says 'I collected the debt and it was lost' and the claimant denies him, then the statement of the agent is taken. As they have explicitly stated. His statement: 'from someone whose testimony is rejected for him' like his origin (father), his branch (son), his husband, his wife, his master, his slave, his mukatab, and his partner in what they share. His statement: 'this is according to Abu Hanifa for him'? Because places of suspicion are excluded from agencies, and this is a place of suspicion evidenced by the non-acceptance of testimony, and because benefits are connected between them, so it becomes a sale from himself from one aspect, unlike mudaraba, for the mudarib is like one acting for himself from one aspect. Do you not see that the owner of capital cannot prevent him from disposal after he has made the capital trade goods, and he is his partner in profit, so the suspicion does not attach to him in selling at like value because he is like one selling his own property. (And the sale of the agent is valid whether small or large, and with commodities, and on credit.) This is according to Abu Hanifa. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): it is not valid except with what people tolerate in mutual exchange, so it is not valid except with dirhams and dinars because the absolute is restricted to the customary, and by 'on credit' is meant sale with deferred payment, and according to the two it is restricted to a customary term. His statement: 'according to the two'—because the agency is unrestricted regarding a specific person, and there is no suspicion in selling at like value because properties are separate and benefits are disconnected. Do you not see that it is permissible for the son to have intercourse with his concubine, and if his ownership were not separate from his father's ownership, it would be a shared concubine, and it would not be permissible for him to have intercourse with her then—unlike the slave, because the sale from his slave is a sale of himself, because what is in the slave's hand belongs to the master, so one person becomes the two parties of the contract, and that is not valid. And the master has a right in the property of his mukatab, and it becomes actual by inability, so it is a sale of himself or a suspicion is present. And it is unlike outright cheating (ghabn fahish). His statement: 'and according to the two it is not valid...'—meaning that according to the two, and it is also the statement of al-Shafi'i, his sale is not valid with a deficiency that people do not tolerate, so it is valid with slight cheating (ghabn yasir), and his sale is not valid except with dirhams and dinars in cash or for a customary term, because the agency for sale occurred absolutely, and the absolute is restricted to the customary, so it is restricted by it. And the secret in it is that transactions were only established to fulfill needs, so agency for transactions is restricted to places of need, and the customary is sale at fair price and with cash or deferred with a customary term among people, and selling something worth one thousand for ten to be paid after one hundred years is not customary. Do you not see that agency to buy charcoal is restricted to the cold days of that year, and agency to buy snow is restricted to the summer days of that year, and agency to buy the sacrificial animal is restricted to the days of sacrifice in that year or before, such that if he buys it in the second year, it is not binding on the principal. This is explicitly stated in al-Inaya and other works.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on al-Wiqaya, expanding on the ruling of an agent (wakil) selling to or buying from persons whose testimony would be rejected for him. The text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Sahibayn). The lesson first defines the scope: it includes not only sale but also lease, currency exchange, salam, and marriage. The agent cannot contract with his own father, child, spouse, master, slave, mukatab, or partner in jointly owned property. Abu Hanifa rules such transactions absolutely invalid because these are 'places of suspicion' (mawadi' al-tuhma) — the parties are so closely connected that the agent is effectively selling to himself; testimonial rejection serves as evidence of this suspicion. By contrast, the Sahibayn distinguish between selling at fair market value (mithl al-qima) and selling below that. They permit selling at fair price because there is no real suspicion — ownerships are separate, as shown by the permissibility of a son sleeping with his own concubine (which would be incest if shared). However, they restrict the agent to selling for cash (dirhams/dinars) or for a customary credit term, since the absolute agency is understood to follow custom. Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with the Sahibayn. The passage also excludes the mudarib (investment agent) when he sells at fair value, as he acts partly for himself. The text concludes with examples showing that agencies are temporally restricted by custom and need.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed by another (principal/muwakkil) to perform a specific transaction on his behalf.
ترد شهادته (turuddu shahadatuhu): A person whose testimony in court is not accepted for the agent due to close relationship (father, son, spouse, etc.).
مضاربة (mudaraba): A silent partnership where one party provides capital and the other labor, with profit sharing.
مثل القيمة (mithl al-qima): The fair market value or a price that does not involve significant undervaluation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), under what condition is an agent's sale to his father valid?
A) Only if the father is not the agent's testator
B) If the sale is at fair market value and for cash or customary credit
C) Never valid, as per all scholars
D) Only if the agent is also a mudarib

Key Takeaway
An agent's sale to close relatives is invalid under Abu Hanifa but permitted by the Sahibayn if at fair market value and with cash or customary credit.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Scope of General Agency: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Custom
Intra-madhhab dispute on agency scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on general agency to determine the validity of an agent's sale, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
A general agent may sell at any price per Abu Hanifa; the two companions restrict to customary value and currency.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when a principal gives an agent unrestricted permission to sell, how far does that authority extend? Abu Hanifa holds that the agent may sell for any price, whether cash or goods, and on any credit term. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that custom (urf) restricts the agent to selling at the customary price and for cash or customary credit. Understanding this difference is crucial for determining when a principal is bound by an agent's transaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The base text states: 'The sale by the agent is valid whether for little or much, and for goods, and on credit.' Recognize this as the starting point before the dispute is introduced.
This is the default statement from the matn, attributed to Abu Hanifa.
2
Contrast with the two companions' position
Note the phrase 'according to the two companions: it is not valid except for what people consider negligible in value, and only with dirhams and dinars.' Identify that they restrict both price and medium of exchange to what is customary.
The two companions also require a customary term for credit sales.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's rationale
Abu Hanifa argues that absolute agency applies unless there is tuhma (suspicion). The agent's property is separate from the principal's, so no conflict of interest exists. A sale at a loss is still a valid sale.
He uses the example of a son's separate ownership of a slave-girl to illustrate distinct interests.
4
Analyze the two companions' rationale
They rely on the principle that an absolute command is restricted by custom (urf). Transactions are meant to fulfill needs, so agency is limited to customary practices. Selling at a gross loss is partly a gift, not a pure sale.
Examples: agency to buy coal is limited to cold months, buying snow to summer, etc.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa, the principal is bound if the agent sells far below market or for goods. Under the two companions, such a sale is invalid and the principal can reject it.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text

وصح بيع الوكيل بما قل أو كثر، والعرض، والنسيئة وعندهما: يجوز إن كان بمثل القيمة إلا من عبده أو مكاتبه. (وصح بيع الوكيل بما قل أو كثر ، والعرض ، والنسيئة)، هذا عند أبي حنيفة ، وعندهما : لا يصح إلا بما يتغابنُ النَّاسُ فيه، فلا يصح إلا بالدراهم والدنانير؛ لأن المطلق ينصرف إلى المتعارف ، والمراد بالنسيئة : البيع بالثمن المؤجل، وعندهما يتقيد بأجل متعارف.

من
[٢] قوله : وعندهما لا يصح ...الخ ؛ يعني إنَّ عندهما وهـو قـول الشافعي له أيضاً ، لا يصح بيعه بنقصان لا يتغابنُ النَّاسُ فيه، فيجوز بالغبن اليسير، ولا يجوز بيعه إلا بالدراهم والدنانير حالة، أو إلى أجل متعارف ؛ لأن التوكيل بالبيع وقع مطلقاً، والمطلق ينصرف إلى المتعارف، فيتقيد به.
والسر فيه : إنَّ التصرفات إنّما وُضِعَتْ لدفع الحاجات، فالتوكيل بالتصرفاتِ تتقيد بمواقع الحاجة، والمتعارفُ هو البيعُ بثمن المثل وبالنقود حالة أو مؤجلة بأجل
متعارف بين الناس، وبيع ما يساوي ألفا بعشرة إلى مئة سنة مثلاً غير متعارف.
ألا ترى أن التوكيل بشراء الفحم يتقيد بأيام البرد في تلك السنة، والتوكيلُ بشراء الحمد بأيام الصيف في تلك السنة، والتوكيل بشراء الأضحية بأيام النحر في تلك السنة أو قبلها، حتى لو اشترى ذلك في السنة الثانية لم يلزم الآمر ، صرح به في «العناية») ،
وغيرها.
(۱) (العناية» (۸): ۷۷).
And the sale by the agent is valid whether for little or much, and for goods, and on credit. And according to the two companions: it is permissible only if it is for the like value, except from his slave or his mukatab. (And the sale by the agent is valid whether for little or much, and for goods, and on credit) – this according to Abu Hanifa. And according to the two companions: it is not valid except for what people consider negligible in value, so it is not valid except with dirhams and dinars; because the absolute is construed according to custom. And what is meant by nasi'ah is sale with a deferred price, and according to the two companions it is restricted to a customary term. [1] His saying: 'according to the two companions' – because the agency is absolute without restriction to a specific person, and there is no suspicion (tuhma) in a sale at the like value because ownership interests are separate and benefits are distinct. Do you not see that it is permissible for a son to have intercourse with his slave-girl, and if his ownership were not separate from his father's, she would be a jointly owned slave-girl and it would not be permissible for him to have intercourse with her? Unlike a slave, because selling from his slave is a sale of himself, since what is in the hand of a slave belongs to the master, so one person becomes the two sides of the contract, and that is not permissible. And the master has a right in the property of his mukatab, and (the contract) is voided by inability to pay, so it becomes a sale from himself or a doubt arises. And unlike gross fraud (al-ghaban al-fahish). [2] His saying: 'and according to the two companions it is not valid... etc.' – meaning that according to the two companions, and also according to al-Shafi'i, his sale is not valid with a deficiency that people do not tolerate, so it is permissible with slight fraud, and his sale is not valid except with dirhams and dinars on the spot, or for a customary term; because the agency to sell occurred absolutely, and the absolute is construed according to custom, so it is restricted by it. And the underlying reason is that transactions were only instituted to fulfill needs, so agency to transact is restricted by the situations of need. And what is customary is selling at the like price and with cash, on the spot or deferred for a customary term among people. Selling something worth a thousand for ten to be paid after a hundred years is not customary. Do you not see that agency to buy charcoal is restricted to the days of cold in that year, and agency to buy snow to days of summer in that year, and agency to buy a sacrificial animal to the days of sacrifice in that year or before it, so that if one buys it in the second year, it is not binding on the principal, as stated in al-'Inaya and others.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental dispute in Hanafi law regarding the scope of a general agent's authority to sell. The base ruling (matn) states that an agent's sale is valid whether for a small or large amount, whether for cash or goods, and whether on credit or spot. However, it immediately notes that this is according to Abu Hanifa; according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the sale is only valid if the price is within the customary range of what people overlook (i.e., slight variation), and only in cash (dirhams and dinars) or on credit with a customary term. The commentary then elaborates on the reasoning. For Abu Hanifa, the absolute agency (tawkil mutlaq) permits any form of sale unless there is a specific suspicion (tuhma) that the agent is favoring himself. The agent is not suspected because the ownership interests of the principal and agent are separate; the agent does not personally benefit from the transaction. The commentary illustrates this with the example of a father and son: a son may have intercourse with his own slave-girl, but if the property were shared, it would be prohibited; similarly, the agent's ownership is distinct. The only exceptions are sales to the agent's own slave or mukatab, because there the agent would be selling to himself or has a conflicting interest. Abu Hanifa also argues that a sale at a gross loss (ghaban fahish) is still a sale in every respect; for example, a person who swears not to sell would break his oath by such a sale. The two companions and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that the absolute is restricted by custom. Since transactions are meant to satisfy needs, the agency is limited to what is customary. Selling at a gross loss is partly a sale and partly a gift. Selling for goods rather than cash is not customary. They provide examples: an agent appointed to buy coal is restricted to buying in the cold season; buying snow is restricted to summer; buying a sacrificial animal is restricted to the days of sacrifice. Therefore, buying outside those seasons does not bind the principal. The dispute has practical implications: according to Abu Hanifa, an agent's sale at a low price or for goods is valid and binding; according to the two companions, such a sale is invalid and the principal may reject it.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakil): The agent appointed by the principal to perform a transaction on his behalf.
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghaban al-fahish): A gross disparity between actual value and sale price, not considered slight.
النسيئة (al-nasi'ah): Deferred payment; sale on credit with a specified future term.
المتعارف (al-muta'araf): What is customary and accepted among people in a given time and place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The price that people customarily tolerate (within slight variation)
C) The exact market price minus 10%
D) Only if the principal approves each sale

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a general agent's sale is valid per Abu Hanifa at any price and for any goods/credit, but the two companions restrict it to customary value and cash, highlighting the role of custom in limiting absolute agency.

Selling Half of Entrusted Goods: Abu Hanifa's Permission
Ruling on partial sale of entrusted goods with intra-madhhab difference on harm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's ruling on an agent selling part of entrusted goods and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding harm in division.

Core Idea
An agent may sell part of the goods unless division causes harm; Abu Hanifa differs from the two companions on harmful cases.

When a principal entrusts an agent to sell a specific commodity, does the agent's authority extend to selling only part of it? This lesson examines the Hanafi positions on partial sale, focusing on the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, over cases where dividing the goods causes harm. Understanding this dispute illuminates how the school balances literal wording with practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and agreement
First, recognize that the case is about an agent appointed to sell a specific item. The question is whether the agent may sell only half. Note the agreement that if division causes no harm (e.g., grains), partial sale is permissible by consensus.
This consensus applies to goods like cereals where splitting does not diminish value.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the agent may sell half even if division causes harm. His proof is that the agency wording is absolute (mutlaq) – 'sell' does not limit to selling all at once. He argues that selling half for half the price is even more beneficial than selling the whole for that price, because the principal retains the remainder.
The absolute nature of the command is central: 'sell' covers partial sale.
3
State the companions' objection
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that if division causes harm (e.g., a plot of land or indivisible item), the agent cannot sell only half because the agency implicitly intends sale of the whole entity. They consider that partial sale when harmful is not within the agent's authority.
They do not differ from Abu Hanifa when division is harmless.
4
Analyze the thamarah (practical consequence)
The practical difference is whether the agent's partial sale is valid or void when the goods cannot be split without loss. Under Abu Hanifa it is valid; under the two companions it is invalid (fasid). The mufta bihi (operative position) is Abu Hanifa's view, though later scholars may caution in cases of clear harm.
This affects the agent's liability and the principal's recourse.
5
Connect to broader Hanafi principles
This dispute reflects a broader methodology: Abu Hanifa prioritizes the literal scope of the command (absolute wording), while the companions consider the implicit objective (avoiding harm). Both approaches are valid within Hanafi usul, leading to a legitimate ikhtilaf.
Similar reasoning appears in issues like gross fraud (ghaban fahish) and barter (muqayada).

Source Text

ولان البيع بغين فاحش بيع من وجه ، وهبة من وجه ؛ ولهذا لو صدر من المريض اعتبر من الثلث، ولا يملكه الأب والوصي، وكذلك المقايضةُ بيع من وجه، وشراء من وجه، فإنه من حيث أن فيه إخراج السلعة من الملك بيع، ومن حيث أن فيه تحصيل السلعة في الملك شراء، فلا يتناوله مطلق اسم البيع.
ووجه قول الإمام : إِنَّ التوكيل بالبيع مطلق، فيجري على إطلاقه في غير موضع التهمة، والبيع بالغبن أو بالعين متعارف عند شدة الحاجة إلى الثمن] والتبرم من العين ، والبيع بغبن فاحش بيع من كل وجه، ألا ترى أن من حلف لا يبيع يحنث بالبيع بغبن
فاحش.

منهما.

Book of Agency, Chapter of Agency for Sale and Purchase. And selling half of what he was entrusted to sell – this according to Abu Hanifa. [2] And because sale with gross fraud is a sale from one aspect and a gift from one aspect; hence if it occurs from a sick person, it is considered from one-third, and the father and executor cannot own it. Similarly, exchange (muqayada) is a sale from one aspect and a purchase from one aspect. So absolute name of sale does not cover it. And the proof of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is that the agency for sale is absolute, so it operates absolutely where there is no suspicion. And sale with fraud or for goods is customary when there is severe need for the price and desire to be rid of the goods. And sale with gross fraud is a sale from every aspect; do you not see that one who swears not to sell breaks his oath by a sale with gross fraud. If you say: If sale with gross fraud were a sale from every aspect, then the father and executor should be able to perform it, but that is not the case. We reply: The father and executor cannot perform it even though it is a sale, because their guardianship over a minor is based on consideration with mercy, and there is no consideration in a sale at a loss. And exchange is a purchase from every aspect with respect to the other party's goods, and a sale from every aspect with respect to one's own goods, because the definition of each applies. [1] His saying: 'half of what he was entrusted to sell' – it is stated in al-Kifayah: 'Verily, selling half of what he was entrusted, when there is no harm in its division, like wheat and barley, is permissible by agreement.' End quote. So it becomes clear that the disagreement is in the case where one was entrusted to sell something whose division is harmful, not in the absolute case. [2] His saying: 'this according to Abu Hanifa' – the proof of his statement is that the word is absolute, not restricted by a condition of separation or union, so it operates absolutely. Do you not see that if he sells the whole for half the price, it is permissible according to him, so if he sells half for half the price, its permissibility is even more likely, because retaining some along with selling some at this price is more beneficial for him than selling the whole at that price.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage discusses a sub-issue: if an agent is appointed to sell a specific property, may he sell only half of it? The matn states that selling half is valid according to Abu Hanifa. The commentary explains that the disagreement is limited to cases where division causes harm (like an indivisible item); in divisible goods like grains, there is consensus. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the agency is absolute and the word 'sell' does not require selling the whole. Selling part of the goods at the same proportional price is actually more beneficial to the principal because he retains part of the property. The commentary also draws a parallel to the earlier discussion of gross fraud: although gross fraud is partly a gift, it is still considered a sale from every aspect for the purpose of oaths. But the father and guardian cannot engage in such sales because their role is to protect the minor, and a loss-making sale is not protective. Similarly, exchange (barter) is both sale and purchase depending on perspective, but the absolute name of sale does not apply to it. The key point is that the agent's authority is based on the absolute wording, and partial sale is included as long as there is no suspicion of self-dealing.

Key Terms
التبعض (al-tab'id): Division of the subject matter into parts; selling only a portion of the entrusted property.
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghaban al-fahish): Gross disparity between price and value; considered partly a gift.

D) Because the two companions agree.

Key Takeaway
The agent's authority to sell part of entrusted goods is permissible under Abu Hanifa's absolute reading of the agency, even when division causes harm; the companions' restriction highlights the role of implicit intent.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Selling Half of Authorized Goods: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agency authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on an agent selling half of the goods, explain the proofs for each, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
An agent may sell half the goods; Abu Hanifa permits it absolutely, the Sahibayn only if the remainder is sold before dispute.

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute about the extent of an agent's authority when authorized to sell. Abu Hanifa takes a literal stance, while the Sahibayn restrict the authorization based on custom and partnership harm. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi jurists balance textual absoluteness with practical considerations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
The issue is whether an agent, authorized to sell a specific item, can sell only half of that item. The dispute only applies when dividing the item causes harm (e.g., an indivisible good).
For divisible goods like wheat, selling half is permissible by consensus.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Proof
Abu Hanifa permits selling half unconditionally. His proof: the authorization is absolute (mutlaq), so it operates fully. Selling half for half the price is more beneficial than selling the whole for half, and qiyas from selling the whole for half price supports this. Harm of partnership is less than selling at a loss.
He also uses the argument that sale at a gross loss is still a sale from every aspect.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not permit selling half initially. Their proof: authorization is directed to the customary practice (urf), and selling half of an indivisible good is not customary. It causes partnership harm, which the agent must avoid.
They consider the agent's act a violation unless remedied.
4
Note the Exception (Istihsan)
The Sahibayn allow the half sale if the agent sells the remaining half before any dispute arises. This is based on istihsan: selling half may be a means to comply with the order when a full sale is not possible. Once the remainder is sold, the initial half sale is validated as a step toward full compliance.
By qiyas, the half sale would be invalid regardless, but istihsan lifts the suspension.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the half sale is immediately valid and binding on the principal. Under the Sahibayn, the half sale is invalid unless the remaining half is sold before dispute; if not, the principal may reject the sale and the agent is liable.
The practical consequence: the agent's risk and the principal's rights differ.

Source Text

كتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء
وبيع نصف ما وُكِّلَ ببيعه) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة )
ولان البيع بغين فاحش بيع من وجه ، وهبة من وجه ؛ ولهذا لو صدر من المريض اعتبر من الثلث، ولا يملكه الأب والوصي، وكذلك المقايضةُ بيع من وجه، وشراء من وجه، فإنه من حيث أن فيه إخراج السلعة من الملك بيع، ومن حيث أن فيه تحصيل السلعة في الملك شراء، فلا يتناوله مطلق اسم البيع.
ووجه قول الإمام : إِنَّ التوكيل بالبيع مطلق، فيجري على إطلاقه في غير موضع التهمة، والبيع بالغبن أو بالعين متعارف عند شدة الحاجة إلى الثمن] والتبرم من العين ، والبيع بغبن فاحش بيع من كل وجه، ألا ترى أن من حلف لا يبيع يحنث بالبيع بغبن فاحش.

Book of Agency, Chapter of Agency for Sale and Purchase. And selling half of what he was authorized to sell — this according to Abu Hanifah. And because the sale at a gross loss is a sale from one perspective and a gift from another; therefore if it occurs from a sick person it is considered from the one-third, and the father and guardian cannot execute it. Likewise, barter is a sale from one perspective and a purchase from another, because it involves removing the commodity from ownership (sale) and acquiring the commodity into ownership (purchase), so the absolute term 'sale' does not encompass it. The face of the Imam's statement: The authorization for sale is absolute, so it operates according to its absoluteness in a place without suspicion, and sale at a loss or for cash is customary when there is severe need for the price and weariness of cash, and sale at a gross loss is a sale from every aspect; do you not see that one who swears not to sell is in breach by selling at a gross loss. If you say: If sale at a gross loss were a sale from every aspect, then the father and guardian should be able to execute it, but the case is not so. We say: The father and guardian cannot execute it even though it is a sale, because their guardianship over the minor is based on consideration with compassion, and there is no consideration in a sale at a loss. And barter is a purchase from every aspect with respect to the other party's commodity, and a sale from every aspect with respect to one's own commodity, because the definition of each is present. [1] His statement: half of what he was authorized to sell. He said in al-Kifayah: Selling half of what he was authorized when there is no harm in dividing it, like wheat and barley, is permissible by agreement. End. So it appears that the dispute is about selling when dividing it causes harm, not in absolute matters. [2] His statement: this according to Abu Hanifah. The face of his statement: The word is absolute, not restricted by the condition of separation or togetherness, so it operates according to its absoluteness. Do you not see that if he sells the whole for half the price, it is permissible by him, so if he sells half for half the price, its permissibility is more apt, because keeping some while selling some at that price is more beneficial to him than selling the whole at that price. If you say: Selling the whole for half the price is permissible because it does not entail the defect of partnership, but selling half entails the defect of partnership in what is harmed by dividing, so this is a violation by the agent towards evil, so his sale should not be binding on the principal. We say: The harm of partnership is lighter and less than the harm of selling the whole for half the price. Since that is permissible according to his statement, the permissibility of this is more apt. Thus they said. His statement: And according to them — and it is the statement of the three Imams — it is not permissible to sell half of what he was authorized to sell, because this sale is not customary and authorization for sale is directed to the customary, and because this sale is a harm of partnership, unless he sells the remaining half before they dispute, i.e., the agent and the principal, because selling half may occur as a means to compliance when the agent cannot find someone who buys the lot, so he needs to divide. If he sells the remaining before litigation and revokes the first sale, it appears that the sale of half occurred as a means to compliance. If he does not sell, it appears that it did not occur as a means to it, so it is not permissible. The conclusion is that selling half after selling the remaining half is permissible, to avoid the harm of partnership. He said in al-Hidayah: This is istihsan according to them. End. And by qiyas it should not be suspended due to the establishment of the half.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an agent selling half of what he was authorized to sell. Abu Hanifa permits it based on the absolute nature of the authorization, arguing that selling half for half the price is more beneficial than selling the whole for half. He rebuts the objection that it causes partnership harm by saying that harm is less than selling all at a loss. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, holding that the authorization is limited to customary practice, and selling half is not customary, and it causes partnership harm. However, they make an exception: if the agent sells the remaining half before any dispute arises, the initial sale of half becomes valid retroactively as a means to fulfill the order. This exception is based on istihsan (juristic preference). The passage also clarifies that the dispute only applies when dividing the goods causes harm; for divisible goods like wheat, it is permissible by consensus. The commentary follows the order of the matn, first presenting Abu Hanifa's view and evidence, then the Sahibayn's view and their istihsan-based concession.

Key Terms
التوكيل (al-tawkeel): The act of authorizing another to perform a legal action on one's behalf.
البيع بالغبن (al-bay' bi'l-ghubn): Sale at a loss, either significant (fahish) or minor.
المقايضة (al-muqayada): Barter: exchange of goods without currency.
عيب الشركة ('ayb al-shirkah): Harm or defect arising from co-ownership, such as needing to share profits or management.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from a clear analogy in favor of a ruling that better serves public interest or avoids hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what condition makes the agent's sale of half the goods permissible?
A) The agent sells the entire goods for half the price.
B) The agent sells the remaining half before any dispute arises.
C) The agent takes a vow not to cause loss.
D) The principal explicitly permits sale of half.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's intra-madhhab dispute on selling half of authorized goods shows how absolute authorization can be restricted by custom and the principle of avoiding harm, with istihsan providing a middle ground.

Agent's Authority to Take a Pledge or Guarantor for the Price
Ruling on agent's authority to take pledge/guarantor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent taking a pledge or guarantor for the price and explain the legal reasoning based on the agent's status as principal in collection.

Core Idea
An agent may take a pledge or guarantor for the price because he is the principal in collecting the debt.

When a seller appoints an agent to sell goods and collect the price, does the agent have authority to secure the price by taking a pledge (rahn) or a guarantor (kafil)? In this lesson, we examine the ruling from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, which confirms that the agent may do so. The reasoning is that the agent stands in the place of the principal regarding rights of recovery, and taking collateral strengthens that process. We also explore an important exception: if the agent himself is not entitled to collect the price (e.g., a minor or slave), he cannot take a pledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The agent's taking of a pledge or guarantor for the price is a legally valid act. The text states it is 'sahih' (valid) and thus permissible.
Focus on the phrase 'صح أخذ الوكيل رهناً' — 'valid is the agent's taking a pledge'.
2
Understand the Legal Reason (Ta'lil)
The agent is considered 'asil fi al-huquq' — principal in rights — regarding collection of the price. Taking a pledge or guarantor strengthens the ability to recover the debt, so the agent possesses this authority.
The principle: the agent's authority extends to acts that facilitate the exercise of his delegated rights.
3
Recognize the Exception
If the agent does not have the right to collect the price himself — for example, if he is a minor (sabi) under interdiction or a slave (abd) under interdiction — then he cannot take a pledge. This is because the condition for this authority is having the right to receive payment.
The text uses 'يشعر بأنّ قبض الثمن لو لم يكن حق الوكيل' — 'this indicates that if collection were not the agent's right...'
4
Confirm the Source of the Ruling
This ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah (corpus juris) and is undisputed within the Hanafi school. It is the mufta bihi (operative position) for fatwa.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is mentioned; the ruling is established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخذه رهناً ، أو كفيلاً بالثَّمن، فلا يضمن إن ضاع في يده

قوله : وأخذه رهنا ...الخ ؛ أي وصـح أخذ الوكيل رهـنـا بالثمن أو كفيلاً بالثمن ؛ لأنَّ الوكيل أصيل في الحقوق وقبض الثمن منها، والكفالة والارتهان مما يؤكدُ جانب الاستيفاء فيملكهما ، وهذا يشعرُ بأنّ قبضَ الثمن لو لم يكن حق الوكيل كما إذا كان صبياً محجوراً أو عبداً محجوراً لم يكن له أخذ الرهن (٢).
قوله : فلا يضمن...الخ ؛ يعني لا يضمن الوكيل الثمن للموكل ، والقيمة
And his taking a pledge or a guarantor for the price, then he is not liable if it is lost in his hand. His statement: and his taking a pledge etc., i.e., the agent's taking a pledge for the price or a guarantor for the price is valid, because the agent is principal in rights and collection of the price, and the guaranty and pledge are among things that strengthen the side of recovery, so he possesses them. This indicates that if collection of the price were not the agent's right, as if he were a minor under interdiction or a slave under interdiction, he would not have the right to take the pledge. His statement: then he is not liable etc., meaning the agent is not liable to the principal for the price, nor the value.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the authority of an agent to take a pledge (rahn) or a guarantor (kafil) for the price of the sold item, and the agent's liability if such collateral is lost in his custody. The commentary explains that the agent is permitted to do so because he is considered the principal (asil) with respect to rights and collection of the price. Taking a pledge or guarantor is an act that strengthens the ability to collect the price, so the agent may do it. However, if the agent himself is not entitled to collect the price (e.g., if he is a minor or a slave under interdiction), then he cannot take a pledge. The passage also clarifies that if the agent takes a pledge or guarantor and it is lost in his custody without negligence, he is not liable to the principal for the price or the value of the collateral. This is because the agent is acting as a trustee (amin) with regard to the collateral, not a guarantor.

Key Terms
الرهن (al-rahn): A pledge or collateral given as security for a debt.
الكفيل (al-kafil): A guarantor or surety who is responsible for the debt if the debtor fails to pay.
الضمان (al-daman): Liability or responsibility to compensate for loss or damage.
الوكيل (al-wakeel): An agent who is authorized to act on behalf of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is an agent allowed to take a pledge or guarantor for the price?
A) Because the agent owns the goods being sold.
B) Because the agent is considered principal in rights of collection.
C) Because the principal has delegated all his rights to the agent.
D) Because the pledge belongs to the agent.

Key Takeaway
An agent may take a pledge or guarantor for the price because he is the principal in collection rights, but only if he himself has the right to collect.

Agent's Liability for Loss of Pledge or Guarantor Held in Trust
Ruling on agent's liability for loss of pledge/guarantor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an agent is not liable for loss of a pledge or guarantor under his custody and apply the principle of trusteeship (amanah).

Core Idea
The agent is a trustee over the pledge; he is not liable for loss unless negligent.

When an agent takes a pledge (rahn) or guarantor (kafil) for the price, what happens if that collateral is lost in his custody? The ruling from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is clear: the agent is not liable (la yadman). This lesson unpacks the legal principle behind this ruling: the agent is considered a trustee (amin) over the collateral, not a guarantor (damin). We also examine the boundary condition where the agent becomes liable due to negligence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Liability
The text states: 'فلا يضمن إن ضاع في يده' — he is not liable if it is lost in his hand. This is the core ruling of the passage.
Focus on the phrase 'فلا يضمن' — 'then he is not liable'.
2
Understand the Legal Status of the Agent
The agent is acting as a trustee (amin) over the pledge. In Hanafi law, an amin is not liable for loss unless there is negligence or transgression (ta'addi). The pledge is held as amanah (trust).
Contrast with a guarantor (damin) who is liable unconditionally.
3
Distinguish Between Amanah and Daman
The agent's possession of the pledge is for the benefit of the principal; the agent does not take ownership or risk. Thus, the default rule is no liability.
This distinction is a key principle in Hanafi muamalat.
4
Identify the Exception for Negligence
The text does not explicitly mention negligence, but it is implicit in the concept of amanah. If the agent fails to exercise due care, he becomes a damin (liable) for the loss.
This is a standard corollary: amanah shifts to daman upon ta'addi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخذه رهناً ، أو كفيلاً بالثَّمن، فلا يضمن إن ضاع في يده

قوله : وأخذه رهنا ...الخ ؛ أي وصـح أخذ الوكيل رهـنـا بالثمن أو كفيلاً بالثمن ؛ لأنَّ الوكيل أصيل في الحقوق وقبض الثمن منها، والكفالة والارتهان مما يؤكدُ جانب الاستيفاء فيملكهما ، وهذا يشعرُ بأنّ قبضَ الثمن لو لم يكن حق الوكيل كما إذا كان صبياً محجوراً أو عبداً محجوراً لم يكن له أخذ الرهن (٢).
قوله : فلا يضمن...الخ ؛ يعني لا يضمن الوكيل الثمن للموكل ، والقيمة
And his taking a pledge or a guarantor for the price, then he is not liable if it is lost in his hand. His statement: and his taking a pledge etc., i.e., the agent's taking a pledge for the price or a guarantor for the price is valid, because the agent is principal in rights and collection of the price, and the guaranty and pledge are among things that strengthen the side of recovery, so he possesses them. This indicates that if collection of the price were not the agent's right, as if he were a minor under interdiction or a slave under interdiction, he would not have the right to take the pledge. Source pages p. 56

Commentary

The commentary explains that the agent is permitted to do so because he is considered the principal (asil) with respect to rights and collection of the price. However, if the agent himself is not entitled to collect the price (e.g., if he is a minor or a slave under interdiction), then he cannot take a pledge. الضمان (al-daman): Liability or responsibility to compensate for loss or damage.

Checkpoint

A) The agent, because he had possession.
B) The principal, because the agent is a trustee.
C) The buyer, because he owned the pledge.
D) The agent, but only if the fire was caused by his negligence.

Key Takeaway
An agent holding a pledge or guarantor is a trustee: he is not liable for loss without negligence.

Selling Half of the Commissioned Item: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Companions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling half of agency item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding an agent selling half of a commodity, explain the reasoning based on qiyas and istihsan, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
An agent may sell half only if the remaining half is also sold before dispute, to avoid partnership harm.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether an agent commissioned to sell a commodity may validly sell only half of it. Abu Hanifa considers it permissible by analogy with selling the whole for half the price. The two companions restrict it, requiring the remaining half to be sold before a dispute arises. Their ruling is based on istihsan to prevent the harm of co-ownership (darar al-shirkah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The issue is whether an agent can validly sell only half of what he was commissioned to sell. Abu Hanifa says yes; the two companions say no unless he also sells the rest before a dispute.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school itself.
2
Trace Abu Hanifa's qiyas argument
Abu Hanifa analogizes: selling the whole for half the price is permissible, so selling half is even more permissible because the harm of partnership is less than the harm of a half-price sale.
This is a qiyas awla (a fortiori) argument.
3
Analyze the companions' istihsan reasoning
The two companions argue that selling half is not customary (ghayr muta'arif) and creates a harmful partnership in a divisible item. They permit it only if the agent sells the remaining half before a dispute, which would show that the first sale was a means to comply with the commission.
This is based on istihsan, departing from strict qiyas.
4
Examine the objection and response
The objection: selling whole for half price does not create partnership, but selling half does. The response: partnership harm is lighter than the harm of a half-price sale, so if whole-for-half is allowed, half is even more allowable.
Abu Hanifa's response is also a qiyas argument.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
The relied-upon position is that of the two companions: the sale of half is invalid unless the remaining half is sold before any dispute. Al-Hidayah presents this as istihsan, implying tarjih.
The mufta bihi is what a mufti would use in fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعندهما : لا يجوز إلا أن يبيع الباقي قبل أن يختصما ؛ لئلا يلزم ضرر الشركة.
فإن قلت : إنما يجوز بيع الكلِّ بثمن النصف ؛ لأنه لم يتضمن عيب الشركة، وأما بيعُ النصف يتضمن عيب الشركة فيما يتضرر بتبعيضه، فكان هذا مخالفـة مـن الوكيل إلى الشر، فينبغي أن لا ينفذ بيعه على الموكل.
قلنا : ضرر الشركةِ أهونُ وأقل من ضرر بيع الكلِّ بنصف الثمن، فلما جاز ذلك على قوله، فجواز هذا أولى. هكذا قالوا.
[١]قوله : وعندهما ; وهو قول الأئمة الثلاثة، لا يجوز بيع نصف ما وكل ببيعه ؛ لأنَّ هذا البيع غير متعارف والتوكيل بالبيع ينصرفُ إلى المتعارف ؛ ولأنَّ هذا البيع ضرر الشركة، إلا أن يبيع النصف الباقي قبل أن يختصما ؛ أي الوكيل والموكل ؛ لأنَّ بيع النصف قد يقع وسيلة إلى الامتثال بأن لا يجد الوكيل من يشتريه جملة، فيحتاج إلى أن يفرق ، فإذا باع الباقي قبل الخصومة ونقض البيع الأول ظهر أن بيع النصف إنّما وقع وسيلة الامتثال ، واذا لم يبع ظهر أنه لم يقع وسيلة إليه، فلا يجوز. والحاصل أن بيع النصف بعد بيع النصف الباقي يجوز، لئلا يلزم ضرر الشركة ، قال في «الهداية» : وهذا استحسان عندهما. انتهى. والقياس أن لا يتوقف لثبوتِ النصف.
And according to them (the two companions): It is not permissible unless he sells the remaining [half] before they dispute, lest the harm of partnership occur. If you say: The sale of the whole for half the price is permissible because it does not entail the defect of partnership, but the sale of half entails the defect of partnership in what is harmed by its division, so this would be a violation by the agent towards the detrimental, so it should not be executed against the principal. We say: The harm of partnership is lighter and less than the harm of selling the whole for half the price, so when that is permissible according to his statement, then the permissibility of this is more appropriate. Thus they said.
[1] His statement: 'And according to them' – it is the statement of the three imams: It is not permissible to sell half of what he was commissioned to sell, because this sale is not customary and the commission for sale applies to the customary; and because this sale entails the harm of partnership, unless he sells the remaining half before they (i.e., the agent and principal) dispute, because the sale of half may occur as a means to comply (with the commission) when the agent does not find anyone to buy it as a whole, so he needs to divide it. If he sells the remaining before the dispute and annuls the first sale, it becomes apparent that the sale of half occurred only as a means to comply; if he does not sell, it becomes apparent that it did not occur as a means, so it is not permissible. The conclusion is that the sale of half after the sale of the remaining half is permissible, lest the harm of partnership occur. He said in Al-Hidayah: This is istihsan according to them. End. And by analogy (qiyas) it should not be conditional due to the establishment of [the sale of] half.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an agent for sale selling only half of the commodity he was commissioned to sell. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that it is not permissible to sell half unless he also sells the remaining half before a dispute arises between agent and principal. Their reasoning: selling half is not customary and it creates a harmful partnership (shirkah) in the ownership of the commodity, since the agent and principal would become co-owners in a divisible item. Abu Hanifa, on the other hand, permits selling half without condition. The text presents an objection: selling the whole for half price is allowed (a known ruling from Abu Hanifa), and that sale does not entail the defect of partnership; but selling half does entail partnership harm, so why should it be allowed? The response is that the harm of partnership is lighter than the harm of selling the whole for half the price; when selling the whole for half is allowed, selling half is even more worthy of permission. The commentary then explains the phrase 'وعندهما' (according to them), attributing it to the three imams (likely the two companions and Zufar or a mistaken reference; the correct intra-Hanafi view is that the two companions hold this position, while Abu Hanifa differs). The conclusion in Al-Hidayah is that this is istihsan (juristic preference) according to the two companions, and by strict analogy (qiyas) the sale of half would not be conditional upon selling the remainder.

Key Terms
ضرر الشركة (darar al-shirkah): Harm or disadvantage arising from co-ownership of a divisible item where division causes loss of value.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of legal reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling, used here by the two companions to permit sale of half after selling the rest.
المتعارف (al-muta'arif): What is customary or commonly practiced in commerce; agency contracts are interpreted according to custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), when is it permissible for an agent to sell half of the commodity?
A) It is always permissible.
B) Only if he sells the remaining half before a dispute with the principal.
C) Only if the principal gives explicit permission.
D) It is never permissible.

Key Takeaway
The two companions' position is the mufta bihi: an agent cannot sell half alone; he must sell the remainder before dispute to avoid partnership harm.

Agent for Sale: Authority to Take a Pawn or Guarantor
Ruling on agent's authority to take a pawn or guarantor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent for sale taking a pawn or guarantor, and explain the underlying distinction between original right and deputyship.

Core Idea
An agent for sale takes securities by original right; an agent for debt collection cannot – the key is the nature of authority.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies a key distinction in agency law: an agent authorized to sell and receive the price (wakil bil-bay') may take a pawn or guarantor as security without explicit permission. The reason is that such an agent acts by original right (asalah) in receiving the price, unlike an agent for debt collection who is merely a deputy. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the nuanced scenario of 'loss' (tawa) when the guarantor dies insolvent after a Maliki judge releases the principal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the agent for sale taking a pawn or guarantor for the price. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) and the agent is not liable for loss.
The text states: 'وصح أخذ الوكيل رهناً' (and the agent's taking a pawn is valid).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is rational: because the agent collects the price by original right (asil), and taking securities strengthens the collection. The text says: 'لأن الوكيل أصيل في الحقوق وقبض الثمن منها'.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The connection: since the agent is asil in receiving the price, he has full authority to do what secures that right, including taking a pawn or guarantor. This contrasts with an agent for debt collection, who is a deputy and thus needs explicit permission.
The phrase 'والكفالة والارتهان مما يؤكد جانب الاستيفاء' shows the rationale.
4
Analyze the loss (tawa) scenario
The passage discusses when the principal suffers loss from the guarantor's insolvency. The preferred view: loss occurs when a Maliki judge releases the principal upon the mere guaranty, then the guarantor dies insolvent. This is 'tawa' (loss) specific to taking a guarantor.
The text says: 'والأوجه أن يراد بالتوى : توى مضاف إلى أخذ الكفيل بأن رفع الأمر إلى قاض يرى براءة الأصيل بنفس الكفالة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخذه رهناً، أو كفيلاً بالثمن، فلا يضمن إن ضاع في يده
[٢]قوله : وأخذه رهنا ...الخ ; أي وصـح أخذ الوكيل رهـنـا بالثمن أو كفيلاً بالثمن ؛ لأنَّ الوكيل أصيل في الحقوق وقبض الثمن منها، والكفالة والارتهان مما يؤكدُ جانب الاستيفاء فيملكهما ، وهذا يشعرُ بأنّ قبضَ الثمن لو لم يكن حق الوكيل كما إذا كان صبياً محجوراً أو عبداً محجوراً لم يكن له أخذ الرهن.
[٣) قوله : فلا يضمن...الخ ؛ يعني لا يضمن الوكيل الثمن للموكل ، والقيمة أو تَوَى ما على الكفيل ) : الضمير في ضاع يرجعُ إلى الرهن. وصورةُ التَّوَى : أن يَرْفَعَ الحادثة إلى قاض يرى براءة الأصيل بنفس الكفالة كما هو مذهب مالك له، فحكم ببراءة الأصيل بنفسه ، ثُمَّ مات الكفيل مفلساً.
(ويقيد شراء الوكيل به للراهن إن ضاعَ الرهن في يده ، أو هلك ما على الكفيل ؛ لأنَّ الهالك في يده كالهالك في يد الموكل. والفرق بين هذا وبين الوكيل بقبض الدين، حيث [لا] يملك أخذ الرهن ولا الكفيل لأنّ الوكيل بقبض الدين يقبضه بالنيابة ؛ ولهذا يملك الموكل نهيه عنه، فلا يملكُ الوكيل أخذهما بلا إذن الموكل ، والوكيل بالبيع يقبض الثمن بالأصالة، ولهذا لا يملك الموكل نهيه عن قبضه، فكان له أخذهما.
[١]قوله : على الكفيل ؛ قيل : المراد من الكفالة هاهنا الحوالة ؛ لأنَّ المنوي يتحقق فيها لا في الكفالة، وقيل: المراد حقيقة الكفالة، والتَّوَى يتحقق فيها بموت الكفيل والمكفول عنه مفلسين وفي «النهاية»: المراد هاهنا تَوَى مضاف إلى أخذ الكفيل ؛ لأنه لو لم يأخذ كفيلاً لم يحصل كما في الرهن والتَّوَى ذكره هنا غير مضاف إلى أخذه الكفيل ؛ لأنه لو لم يأخذ كفيلاً أيضا لتَوَى بموت من عليه الدين، وحمله على الحوالة فاسدٌ ؛ لأنَّ الدِّينَ لا يَثوى فيها بموت المحال عليه مفلساً، بل به يرجع على المحيل، وإنما ينوي بموتهما مفلسين، فصار كالكفالة.
والأوجه أن يراد بالتوى : توى مضاف إلى أخذ الكفيل بأن رفع الأمر إلى قاض يرى براءة الأصيل بنفس الكفالة، كما هو مذهب مالك ، فيحكم ببراءة الأصيل ثم مات الكفيل مفلس (١).
And his taking a pawn or a guarantor for the price, so he is not liable if it is lost in his hand.
[2] His statement: 'And his taking a pawn...' i.e., the agent's taking a pawn for the price or a guarantor for the price is valid, because the agent is an original party in rights and receiving the price from them, and suretyship and pawning are among things that strengthen the side of collection, so he has authority over them. And this indicates that if receiving the price were not the agent's right, as when he is a minor under guardianship or a slave under guardianship, he would not have the right to take the pawn.
[3] His statement: 'So he is not liable...' i.e., the agent is not liable for the price to the principal, and the value or loss of what is upon the guarantor. The pronoun in 'is lost' refers to the pawn. The scenario of loss (tawa) is that he brings the case to a judge who holds that the principal is exonerated by the mere suretyship, as is the school of Malik, so he rules for the exoneration of the principal, then the guarantor dies insolvent.
(And the restriction of the agent's purchase for the pledgor if the pawn is lost in his hand, or what is upon the guarantor perishes, because what perishes in his hand is like what perishes in the hand of the principal. And the difference between this and an agent for debt collection, where he does not have the right to take a pawn or a guarantor, because the agent for debt collection receives by deputyship; therefore the principal has the right to forbid him from it, so the agent does not have the right to take them without the principal's permission. But the agent for sale receives the price by original right, therefore the principal does not have the right to forbid him from receiving it, so he has the right to take them.
[1] His statement: 'upon the guarantor' – it is said: what is meant by suretyship here is assignment (hawala), because loss occurs in it but not in suretyship; and it is said: what is meant is actual suretyship, and loss occurs in it by the death of the guarantor and the guaranteed being insolvent. And in Al-Nihayah: what is meant here is loss added to taking the guarantor, because if he did not take a guarantor, it would not occur as in the pawn; and loss mentioned here is not added to taking the guarantor, because if he also did not take a guarantor, loss would also occur by the death of the debtor. And interpreting it as assignment is invalid because a debt does not become lost in it by the death of the transferee insolvent; rather, one returns upon the transferor; loss only occurs by both dying insolvent, so it becomes like suretyship.
The most likely view is that what is meant by loss is loss added to taking the guarantor, by bringing the case to a judge who holds that the principal is exonerated by the mere suretyship, as is the school of Malik, so he rules for the exoneration of the principal, then the guarantor dies insolvent.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that an agent for sale (wakil bil-bay') may take a pawn (rahn) or a guarantor (kafil) for the price he is to collect, and if the pawn is lost or the guarantor becomes insolvent, the agent is not liable to the principal for the price. The reason is that the agent for sale receives the price by original right (bil-asalah), not merely as a deputy (bil-niyabah). This is contrasted with an agent for debt collection (wakil bi-qabd al-dayn), who collects by deputyship and therefore cannot take a pawn or guarantor without explicit permission. The agent's right to take these securities stems from his independence in executing the sale and collecting the price. The passage then clarifies the meaning of 'tawa' (loss) in the context of the guarantor. The preferred interpretation is that the loss occurs when the case is brought before a judge who follows the Maliki school, which holds that the mere act of guaranty releases the principal, and then the guarantor dies insolvent. This scenario is referred to as 'tawa' (loss) of what is upon the guarantor. The passage also discusses alternative interpretations, such as that 'kafalah' here actually means 'hawalah' (assignment) or that it is true suretyship, but ultimately favors the view that it is loss added to taking the guarantor, consistent with the earlier ruling on pawn.

Key Terms
الوكيل بالبيع (al-wakil bi al-bay'): The agent for sale who is authorized both to sell and to receive the price.
أصيل (asil): One who acts in his own right, not as a deputy; the agent for sale is considered an asil in receiving the price.
توى (tawa): Loss that occurs when the guarantor dies insolvent after a judge following Maliki school releases the principal upon the mere act of guaranty.
حوالة (hawalah): Assignment of debt; the passage discusses whether the term 'kafalah' in the text really means 'hawalah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can an agent for sale take a pawn or guarantor for the price without explicit permission from the principal, while an agent for debt collection cannot?
A) Because the agent for sale is more trustworthy.
B) Because the agent for sale receives the price by original right (bil-asalah), while the agent for debt collection receives by deputyship (bil-niyabah).
C) Because the agent for sale has a written contract.
D) Because the agent for debt collection is always supervised.

Key Takeaway
An agent for sale may take a pawn or guarantor without permission because he receives the price by original right, and he is not liable for loss of the pawn or guarantor's insolvency.
